         </span>
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          7 January 1988
         </span>
         *
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       With a mission to provide programmes for all licence-fee payers, it has sport, news, current affairs, and documentaries. It has historically broadcast children's programmes (now taken from
       <a href="/wiki/CBBC" title="CBBC">
        CBBC
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/CBeebies" title="CBeebies">
        CBeebies
       </a>
       ). The channel remains one of the principal television channels in the United Kingdom and provides 2,508 annual hours of news and weather, 1,880 hours of factual and learning, 1,036 hours of drama, 672 hours of children's, 670 hours of sport, 654 hours of film, 433 hours of entertainment, 159 hours of current affairs, 92 hours of religion and 82 hours of music and arts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since 1990 the BBC has had to commission output from other domestic suppliers. Although the statutory target remains 25% for independent production companies to contribute programming for BBC One, 33% of output was made by them in 2010–11.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnnRep2010_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AnnRep2010-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The quota of original programming in peak times is set at 90%, however 100% of peak programming was original in 2010–11.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnnRep2010_87-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AnnRep2010-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Over the whole day, the total for the same year was 89%, against a quota of 70%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnnRep2010_87-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-AnnRep2010-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       2,508 annual hours of news and weather (293 in peak, 1,049 of
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">
        BBC News
       </a>
       simulcasts) are provided by regular news programmes
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Breakfast" title="BBC Breakfast">
         BBC Breakfast
        </a>
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_at_One" title="BBC News at One">
         BBC News at One
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_at_Six" title="BBC News at Six">
         BBC News at Six
        </a>
       </i>
       and the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_at_Ten" title="BBC News at Ten">
         BBC News at Ten
        </a>
       </i>
       each including BBC regional news programmes. All three main news bulletins have a lead over their rival programmes on ITV and other terrestrial or cable channels. During the weekend period, three separate bulletins around these three time periods are broadcast and vary in length from 10–25 minutes. BBC One has broadcast overnight simulcasts from the
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_(TV_channel)" title="BBC News (TV channel)">
        BBC News Channel
       </a>
       since 1997; the latter in turn simulcasts the majority of all regular BBC One bulletins.
      </p>
      <p>
       Each year 159 hours of current affairs programmes are broadcast on BBC One, including
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Panorama_(TV_series)" title="Panorama (TV series)">
         Panorama
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Watchdog_(TV_series)" title="Watchdog (TV series)">
         Watchdog
        </a>
       </i>
       . Politics is also covered, with programmes including
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Question_Time_(TV_series)" title="Question Time (TV series)">
         Question Time
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/This_Week_(BBC_TV_series)" title="This Week (BBC TV series)">
         This Week
        </a>
       </i>
       shown.
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Crimewatch" title="Crimewatch">
         Crimewatch
        </a>
       </i>
       , a programme appealing for help in unsolved crimes, is broadcast monthly.
      </p>
      <p>
       BBC One shows 1,880 hours of factual and learning programming annually. This includes a wide range of shows such as nature documentaries such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Planet_Earth_(franchise)" title="Planet Earth (franchise)">
         Planet Earth
        </a>
       </i>
       as well as lifestyle-format daytime programmes and a number of
       <i>
        reality television
       </i>
       formats and the
       <i>
        One Life
       </i>
       strand.
      </p>
      <p>
       BBC One broadcasts 1,036 hours of drama each year, more than any other BBC channel. There are four half-hour episodes of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/EastEnders" title="EastEnders">
         EastEnders
        </a>
       </i>
       each week (not shown on Wednesdays), with an
       <a href="/wiki/Omnibus_(broadcast)" title="Omnibus (broadcast)">
        omnibus
       </a>
       episode at the weekend, plus hospital dramas
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Casualty_(TV_series)" title="Casualty (TV series)">
         Casualty
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Holby_City" title="Holby City">
         Holby City
        </a>
       </i>
       . Other popular dramas on BBC One include crime dramas such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/New_Tricks" title="New Tricks">
         New Tricks
        </a>
       </i>
       , a programme of which even episode repeats have beaten ITV ratings on numerous occasions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnnRep2006_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AnnRep2006-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       BBC One has traditionally been the home of children's television:
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Blue_Peter" title="Blue Peter">
         Blue Peter
        </a>
       </i>
       had been broadcast on the channel prior to the Children's BBC strand, and sections such as the pre-school
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Watch_with_Mother" title="Watch with Mother">
         Watch with Mother
        </a>
       </i>
       being transmitted on the channel for several decades. This became more pronounced with the launch of Children's BBC, later renamed "
       <a href="/wiki/CBBC" title="CBBC">
        CBBC
       </a>
       ". This new strand was broadcast primarily on BBC One in the late afternoons, as well as Saturday and Sunday mornings also such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Going_Live!" title="Going Live!">
         Going Live!
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Live_%26_Kicking" title="Live &amp; Kicking">
         Live &amp; Kicking
        </a>
       </i>
       , each lasting two to three hours. The launch in 2002 of dedicated digital channels for this content —the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CBBC_Channel" title="CBBC Channel">
        CBBC Channel
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/CBeebies" title="CBeebies">
        CBeebies
       </a>
       —did not affect this provision. Combined with BBC Two, the channel broadcast 2,195 hours of children's programmes in 2010, mostly in the late afternoons on weekdays.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnnRep2010_87-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-AnnRep2010-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Saturday morning children's programming moved to BBC Two in 2006 following a three-month trial.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Sports coverage on BBC One includes
       <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">
        Premier League
       </a>
       football highlights on
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Match_of_the_Day" title="Match of the Day">
         Match of the Day
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">
        The Championships, Wimbledon
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/London_Marathon" title="London Marathon">
        London Marathon
       </a>
       , and other international
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" title="Athletics (sport)">
        athletics
       </a>
       and swimming events, the
       <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">
        Olympic Games
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rugby_League" title="Rugby League">
        Rugby League
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rugby_Union" title="Rugby Union">
        Rugby Union
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Snooker" title="Snooker">
        Snooker
       </a>
       tournaments and more.
      </p>
      <p>
       The BBC showed the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">
        2010 FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       , splitting the group stage matches with ITV. The BBC had first pick of matches from the second round. Repeats made up 8.4% of peak programming in 2010–11, up from 8.0% for 2008–09.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnnRep2010_87-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-AnnRep2010-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Programming on this channel costs an average of £162,900 per hour.
      </p>
      <p>
       British and international films are broadcast for 654 hours each year on BBC One. This is mainly late-night fillers with some box office hits at Christmas and holiday periods. Sometimes on a Saturday afternoon there is a film on to fill the gap between entertainment shows but very rarely has there been one in that slot.
      </p>
      <p>
       Entertainment programming on BBC One includes game shows such as the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/National_Lottery_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Lottery (United Kingdom)">
         National Lottery
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Total_Wipeout" title="Total Wipeout">
         Total Wipeout
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Strictly_Come_Dancing" title="Strictly Come Dancing">
         Strictly Come Dancing
        </a>
       </i>
       and chat shows such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Graham_Norton_Show" title="The Graham Norton Show">
         The Graham Norton Show
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The annual 92 hours of religious programming comprise weekly editions of live
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Songs_of_Praise" title="Songs of Praise">
         Songs of Praise
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
        Christian
       </a>
       services and other shows from independent production companies. Mentorn Oxford produces
       <i>
        Heart and Soul
       </i>
       , described as "a new multi-faith programme featuring a panel and a studio audience", followed by
       <i>
        Life from the Loft
       </i>
       which is made by the Leeds-based company True North.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2005 BBC One was criticised for reducing the amount of religious programming, previously 101 hours per year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       BBC One broadcasts many comedy programmes, often on Friday nights. These have included the stand-up comedy show
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Live_at_the_Apollo_(TV_series)" title="Live at the Apollo (TV series)">
         Live at the Apollo
        </a>
       </i>
       , sitcom
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Outnumbered_(UK_TV_series)" title="Outnumbered (UK TV series)">
         Outnumbered
        </a>
       </i>
       , and satirical quiz show
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Have_I_Got_News_for_You" title="Have I Got News for You">
         Have I Got News for You
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Saturday evening is also a popular slot for a comedy show such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Michael_McIntyre%27s_Big_Show" title="Michael McIntyre's Big Show">
         Michael McIntyre's Big Show
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Armstrong_and_Miller_Show" title="The Armstrong and Miller Show">
         The Armstrong and Miller Show
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       As the weekly popular music chart programme
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">
         Top of the Pops
        </a>
       </i>
       was dropped in 2006 (except for the Christmas Day edition), BBC One broadcast 49 hours of music and arts programming in 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnnRep2010_87-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-AnnRep2010-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The majority of this was
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Imagine_(TV_series)" title="Imagine (TV series)">
         Imagine
        </a>
       </i>
       , presented by
       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Yentob" title="Alan Yentob">
        Alan Yentob
       </a>
       , and classical music concerts, in particular some of the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Proms" title="BBC Proms">
         BBC Proms
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       BBC One's daytime line-up was a major factor in it overtaking ITV as the most popular channel in 2000, a position it has retained, even though ITV achieves a higher audience share during the daytime.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The morning daytime line-up consists of lifestyle shows, such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Homes_Under_the_Hammer" title="Homes Under the Hammer">
         Homes Under the Hammer
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Bargain_Hunt" title="Bargain Hunt">
         Bargain Hunt
        </a>
       </i>
       , the afternoons contain drama with daily soap
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Doctors_(2000_TV_series)" title="Doctors (2000 TV series)">
         Doctors
        </a>
       </i>
       and classic US drama, such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Diagnosis:_Murder" title="Diagnosis: Murder">
         Diagnosis: Murder
        </a>
       </i>
       . Sometimes a drama such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Land_Girls_(TV_series)" title="Land Girls (TV series)">
         Land Girls
        </a>
       </i>
       is shown in the afternoons.
      </p>
      <p>
       Between 15:05 and 17:05 was the CBeebies/CBBC broadcasting strand, with its own visual identity. Historically, BBC One's most popular daytime programme was
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Neighbours" title="Neighbours">
         Neighbours
        </a>
       </i>
       , with audience figures approaching five million. On 11 February 2008, BBC One dropped
       <i>
        Neighbours
       </i>
       and the programme has since been broadcast on
       <a href="/wiki/Channel_5_(UK)" title="Channel 5 (UK)">
        Channel 5
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In its place the quiz show
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Weakest_Link_(UK_game_show)" title="The Weakest Link (UK game show)">
         The Weakest Link
        </a>
       </i>
       , moved from BBC Two, later replaced in 2011 by
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pointless" title="Pointless">
         Pointless
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       On 16 May 2012, the BBC announced the children's block of shows would be moved permanently to CBBC and CBeebies upon the completion of the Digital switchover.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In its place appear the game show
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Perfection_(game_show)" title="Perfection (game show)">
         Perfection
        </a>
       </i>
       , plus
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Escape_to_the_Country" title="Escape to the Country">
         Escape to the Country
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Put_Your_Money_Where_Your_Mouth_Is_(TV_series)" title="Put Your Money Where Your Mouth Is (TV series)">
         Put Your Money Where Your Mouth Is
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Presentation">
        Presentation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_One&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Presentation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_BBC_television_idents#BBC_Television_Service/BBC_One" title="History of BBC television idents">
        History of BBC television idents
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_One_circle.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="236" data-file-width="422" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ca/BBC_One_circle.jpg/220px-BBC_One_circle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ca/BBC_One_circle.jpg/330px-BBC_One_circle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/ca/BBC_One_circle.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBC_One_circle.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The BBC One 'Hippos' ident (2006-16)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       BBC One's identity has been symbolised by a globe shown on its
       <a href="/wiki/Station_identification" title="Station identification">
        idents
       </a>
       for much of its existence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first BBC One ident was shown on 2 December 1953, known as the Bat's Wings. In 1962 this was replaced by a map of the UK shown between programmes, and in 1963 the globe appeared, changing in style and appearance over the next 39 years.
      </p>
      <p>
       Most notably, on 18 February 1985, the "
       <a href="/wiki/Computer_Originated_World" title="Computer Originated World">
        Computer Originated World
       </a>
       " was introduced. This was a computer-animated globe with the land coloured gold and the sea a transparent blue, giving the impression of a glass globe. This was replaced by the "
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_One_%27Virtual_Globe%27_ident" title="BBC One 'Virtual Globe' ident">
        Virtual Globe
       </a>
       " on 16 February 1991. On 4 October 1997, the globe became a
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_One_%27Balloon%27_idents" title="BBC One 'Balloon' idents">
        red, orange and yellow hot-air balloon
       </a>
       , coloured to resemble a globe. It was filmed flying around various places in the UK.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_One_%27Oneness%27_Exercise_Class_Ident.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="236" data-file-width="421" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a2/BBC_One_%27Oneness%27_Exercise_Class_Ident.jpg/220px-BBC_One_%27Oneness%27_Exercise_Class_Ident.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a2/BBC_One_%27Oneness%27_Exercise_Class_Ident.jpg/330px-BBC_One_%27Oneness%27_Exercise_Class_Ident.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a2/BBC_One_%27Oneness%27_Exercise_Class_Ident.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBC_One_%27Oneness%27_Exercise_Class_Ident.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The BBC One 'Exercise Class' ident (2017-present)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 29 March 2002 the globe was replaced by a series of visual identities, "idents", consisting of people
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_One_%27Rhythm_%26_Movement%27_idents" title="BBC One 'Rhythm &amp; Movement' idents">
        dancing in various styles
       </a>
       . These were replaced on 7 October 2006 by the
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_One_%27Circle%27_idents" title="BBC One 'Circle' idents">
        'circle' idents
       </a>
       . According to the BBC, the circle symbol both represents togetherness (unity) and acts as a link to the classic globe icon used for 39 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They ran until 4 December 2016, when that year's Christmas idents launched. On 1 January 2017, a
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_One_%27Oneness%27_idents" title="BBC One 'Oneness' idents">
        new ident set
       </a>
       launched, based on the theme of "oneness".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_variations">
        Regional variations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_One&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Regional variations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       BBC One has individual continuity and opt-outs for
       <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">
        Scotland
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">
        Wales
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">
        Northern Ireland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Each variant maintains the BBC One logo with the addition of the country name beneath it.
      </p>
      <p>
       In England,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       each region has an individual
       <a href="/wiki/Category:BBC_Regional_News_programmes" title="Category:BBC Regional News programmes">
        regional news
       </a>
       and current affairs programme opt-out as well as a limited amount of continuity. During these opt-outs, the region name is displayed as with the national variations, beneath the main channel logo.
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/UK_Today" title="UK Today">
         UK Today
        </a>
       </i>
       , a news programme, was shown nationally to digital viewers in place of regional programmes when they were unavailable to broadcast on analogue television. The programme was discontinued in 2002 and replaced by a transmission of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/BBC_London_News" title="BBC London News">
         BBC London News
        </a>
       </i>
       until all BBC regions were made available digitally.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_One_Scotland" title="BBC One Scotland">
        BBC One Scotland
       </a>
       has the greatest level of variation from the generic network, owing to
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Scotland" title="BBC Scotland">
        BBC Scotland
       </a>
       scheduling Scottish programming on the main BBC Scotland channel, rather than on
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">
        BBC Two
       </a>
       . BBC One Scotland variations include the soap opera
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/River_City" title="River City">
         River City
        </a>
       </i>
       and the football programme
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Sportscene" title="Sportscene">
         Sportscene
        </a>
       </i>
       , the inclusion of which causes network programming to be displaced or replaced.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_One_Wales" title="BBC One Wales">
        BBC One Wales
       </a>
       was considered a separate channel by the BBC as early as its launch in the mid-1960s, appearing as BBC Wales.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Availability_outside_the_UK">
        Availability outside the UK
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_One&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Availability outside the UK">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       BBC One (Northern Ireland) is widely available in the
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">
        Republic of Ireland
       </a>
       on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cable_television_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Cable television in the Republic of Ireland">
        cable
       </a>
       and satellite television. BBC One is also available on cable and
       <a href="/wiki/IPTV" title="IPTV">
        IPTV
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Netherlands
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">
        Belgium
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Switzerland
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">
        Liechtenstein
       </a>
       . On 27 March 2013 it was offered by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BFBS" title="BFBS">
        British Forces Broadcasting Service (BFBS)
       </a>
       to members of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Forces" title="Her Majesty's Forces">
        HM Forces
       </a>
       and their families around the world, replacing the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BFBS#BFBS_Television" title="BFBS">
        BFBS1
       </a>
       TV channel, which already carried a selection of BBC One programmes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Accessibility">
        Accessibility
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_One&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Accessibility">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The BBC announced in May 2008 that it had achieved its aim for all programming to have
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtitles" title="Subtitles">
        subtitles
       </a>
       for viewers with hearing difficulties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The BBC also offers
       <a href="/wiki/Audio_description" title="Audio description">
        audio description
       </a>
       on some popular BBC One programmes
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       for visually impaired-viewers. The percentage of the BBC's total television output with audio description available is 10%, having been increased from 8% in 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Controllers_of_BBC_One">
